<p><i><b>The Wizard of Oz</b></i> is a 1939 American <a href="/wiki/Musical_film" title="Musical film">musical</a> <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">fantasy film</a> produced by <a href="/wiki/Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer" title="Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer">Metro-Goldwyn-Mayer</a>. Widely considered to be one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_considered_the_best" title="List of films considered the best">greatest films in cinema history</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> it is the best-known and most commercially successful adaptation of <a href="/wiki/L._Frank_Baum" title="L. Frank Baum">L. Frank Baum</a>'s 1900 children's book, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wonderful_Wizard_of_Oz" title="The Wonderful Wizard of Oz">The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fricke_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fricke-6">[6]</a></sup></i> It stars <a href="/wiki/Judy_Garland" title="Judy Garland">Judy Garland</a> as <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Gale" title="Dorothy Gale">Dorothy Gale</a>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Ray_Bolger" title="Ray Bolger">Ray Bolger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Haley" title="Jack Haley">Jack Haley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bert_Lahr" title="Bert Lahr">Bert Lahr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Morgan" title="Frank Morgan">Frank Morgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Billie_Burke" title="Billie Burke">Billie Burke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Hamilton_(actress)" title="Margaret Hamilton (actress)">Margaret Hamilton</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Charley_Grapewin" title="Charley Grapewin">Charley Grapewin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pat_Walshe" title="Pat Walshe">Pat Walshe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clara_Blandick" title="Clara Blandick">Clara Blandick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terry_(dog)" title="Terry (dog)">Terry</a> (billed as Toto), and the <a href="/wiki/Leo_Singer" title="Leo Singer">Singer Midgets</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Munchkin" title="Munchkin">Munchkins</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Notable for its use of <a href="/wiki/Technicolor" title="Technicolor">Technicolor</a>, fantasy storytelling, musical score, and memorable characters, it has become an icon of American popular culture. It was nominated for six <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a>, but lost to <i><a href="/wiki/Gone_with_the_Wind_(film)" title="Gone with the Wind (film)">Gone with the Wind</a></i>. It did win in two other categories, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Song" title="Academy Award for Best Original Song">Best Original Song</a> for "<a href="/wiki/Over_the_Rainbow" title="Over the Rainbow">Over the Rainbow</a>" and <a href="/wiki/12th_Academy_Awards" title="12th Academy Awards">Best Original Score</a> by <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Stothart" title="Herbert Stothart">Herbert Stothart</a>. While the film was considered a critical success upon release in August 1939, it failed to generate profit for MGM, earning only $3,017,000 on a $2,777,000 budget, which made it MGM's most expensive production to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mannix_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mannix-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The 1956 <a href="/wiki/The_Wizard_of_Oz_on_television" title="The Wizard of Oz on television">broadcast television premiere of the film</a> on the <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> network reintroduced the film to the wider public and eventually made the presentation an annual tradition, making it one of the best known films in movie history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fricke_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Fricke-6">[6]</a></sup> The film was named the most-viewed motion picture on television syndication by the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a>, which also included the film in its <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Registry" title="National Film Registry">National Film Registry</a> in its inaugural year in 1989. Designation on the registry calls for efforts to preserve it for being "culturally, historically, and aesthetically significant".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> It is also one of the few films on <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme#Memory_of_the_World_Register" title="Memory of the World Programme">Memory of the World Register</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Wizard of Oz</i> is the source of many quotes referenced in contemporary <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a>. It was directed primarily by <a href="/wiki/Victor_Fleming" title="Victor Fleming">Victor Fleming</a> (who left production to take over direction on the troubled <i>Gone with the Wind</i> production). <a href="/wiki/Noel_Langley" title="Noel Langley">Noel Langley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence_Ryerson" title="Florence Ryerson">Florence Ryerson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Allan_Woolf" title="Edgar Allan Woolf">Edgar Allan Woolf</a> received credit for the screenplay, but uncredited contributions were made by others. The songs were written by <a href="/wiki/Yip_Harburg" title="Yip Harburg">Edgar "Yip" Harburg</a> (lyrics) and <a href="/wiki/Harold_Arlen" title="Harold Arlen">Harold Arlen</a> (music). The musical score and the incidental music were composed by Stothart.</p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Wizard_of_Oz_Judy_Garland_Terry_1939.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="774" data-file-width="587" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/The_Wizard_of_Oz_Judy_Garland_Terry_1939.jpg/170px-The_Wizard_of_Oz_Judy_Garland_Terry_1939.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/The_Wizard_of_Oz_Judy_Garland_Terry_1939.jpg/255px-The_Wizard_of_Oz_Judy_Garland_Terry_1939.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/The_Wizard_of_Oz_Judy_Garland_Terry_1939.jpg/340px-The_Wizard_of_Oz_Judy_Garland_Terry_1939.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Wizard_of_Oz_Judy_Garland_Terry_1939.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stars Judy Garland as Dorothy Gale and <a href="/wiki/Terry_(dog)" title="Terry (dog)">Terry The Dog</a>, as Toto</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Wizard_of_Oz_Margaret_Hamilton_Judy_Garland_1939.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="467" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/The_Wizard_of_Oz_Margaret_Hamilton_Judy_Garland_1939.jpg/170px-The_Wizard_of_Oz_Margaret_Hamilton_Judy_Garland_1939.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/The_Wizard_of_Oz_Margaret_Hamilton_Judy_Garland_1939.jpg/255px-The_Wizard_of_Oz_Margaret_Hamilton_Judy_Garland_1939.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/The_Wizard_of_Oz_Margaret_Hamilton_Judy_Garland_1939.jpg/340px-The_Wizard_of_Oz_Margaret_Hamilton_Judy_Garland_1939.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Wizard_of_Oz_Margaret_Hamilton_Judy_Garland_1939.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Margaret Hamilton as The Wicked Witch of the West with Dorothy Gale</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The film begins in <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a>, which is depicted in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sepia_tone" title="Sepia tone">sepia tone</a>. Dorothy Gale lives with her dog, <a href="/wiki/Toto_(Oz)" title="Toto (Oz)">Toto</a>, on her <a href="/wiki/Aunt_Em" title="Aunt Em">Aunt Em</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uncle_Henry_(Oz)" title="Uncle Henry (Oz)">Uncle Henry</a>'s farm. Toto gets in trouble with a mean neighbor, Miss Almira Gulch, when he bites her. However, Dorothy's family and the farmhands are all too busy to listen to her troubles. Miss Gulch produces an order from the sheriff allowing her to have Toto <a href="/wiki/Animal_euthanasia" title="Animal euthanasia">put down</a>. She takes him away, but he escapes and returns to Dorothy who, fearing that Miss Gulch will return, decides to run away from home.</p>
<p>After some miles Dorothy and Toto encounter Professor Marvel, a kindly fortune teller who, realizing Dorothy has run away, uses his crystal ball to convince her that Aunt Em is ill. Dorothy races home just as a <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornado</a> approaches. Locked out of the <a href="/wiki/Storm_cellar" title="Storm cellar">storm cellar</a>, she seeks safety in the house, where a wind-blown window sash knocks her out. She awakens to find the tornado has sent the house spinning into the sky. Outside the window she sees farm animals, an old lady knitting in a chair, two men rowing a boat, and finally Miss Gulch, who transforms into a cackling <a href="/wiki/Wicked_Witch_of_the_East" title="Wicked Witch of the East">witch</a> riding a broomstick.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Billie_Burke_and_Judy_Garland_The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="960" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Billie_Burke_and_Judy_Garland_The_Wizard_of_Oz_%281939%29.jpg/170px-Billie_Burke_and_Judy_Garland_The_Wizard_of_Oz_%281939%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Billie_Burke_and_Judy_Garland_The_Wizard_of_Oz_%281939%29.jpg/255px-Billie_Burke_and_Judy_Garland_The_Wizard_of_Oz_%281939%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Billie_Burke_and_Judy_Garland_The_Wizard_of_Oz_%281939%29.jpg/340px-Billie_Burke_and_Judy_Garland_The_Wizard_of_Oz_%281939%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Billie_Burke_and_Judy_Garland_The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dorothy (<a href="/wiki/Judy_Garland" title="Judy Garland">Judy Garland</a>, right) with <a href="/wiki/Glinda_the_Good_Witch" title="Glinda the Good Witch">Glinda the Good Witch of the North</a> (<a href="/wiki/Billie_Burke" title="Billie Burke">Billie Burke</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Suddenly the house strikes the ground and all is quiet. As Dorothy opens the door the film changes to <a href="/wiki/Technicolor" title="Technicolor">Technicolor</a> – she and Toto have landed in <a href="/wiki/Munchkin_Country" title="Munchkin Country">Munchkinland</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Land_of_Oz" title="Land of Oz">Land of Oz</a>. <a href="/wiki/Glinda_the_Good_Witch" title="Glinda the Good Witch">Glinda the Good Witch of the North</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Munchkin" title="Munchkin">Munchkins</a> welcome her as their heroine – the house has landed on and killed the Wicked Witch of the East, leaving only her feet poking out from under. In the middle of the celebration, the <a href="/wiki/Wicked_Witch_of_the_West" title="Wicked Witch of the West">Wicked Witch of the West</a> arrives in a ball of smoke and fire to claim her sister's <a href="/wiki/Ruby_slippers" title="Ruby slippers">ruby slippers</a>, but Glinda transports them onto Dorothy's feet before the witch can get them. The witch swears revenge on Dorothy for her sister's death. Glinda tells Dorothy to follow the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_brick_road" title="Yellow brick road">yellow brick road</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Emerald_City" title="Emerald City">Emerald City</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/Wizard_of_Oz_(character)" title="Wizard of Oz (character)">Wizard of Oz</a> might be able to help her get back home.</p>
<p>On her way, Dorothy meets and befriends a <a href="/wiki/Scarecrow_(Oz)" title="Scarecrow (Oz)">Scarecrow</a>, who wants a brain, and invites him to join her on her journey. Eventually they come to an apple orchard where they find and befriend a <a href="/wiki/Tin_Woodman" title="Tin Woodman">Tin Man</a>, who desires a heart. After they invite him to come along, the Witch appears and makes threats to them. Deep in the woods, they meet a <a href="/wiki/Cowardly_Lion" title="Cowardly Lion">Cowardly Lion</a>, who is in need of courage and invite him to come along as well. After the Witch attempts to stop them using an enchanted poppy field, they finally reach the Emerald City. Inside, after being initially rejected, they are permitted to see the Wizard, who appears as a large disembodied head surrounded by fire. He agrees to grant their wishes when they bring him the Witch of the West's broomstick, implying they must kill her to get it.</p>
<p>On their journey to the Witch's castle, they pass through the Haunted Forest, while the Witch views their progress in her crystal ball. She sends her <a href="/wiki/Winged_monkeys" title="Winged monkeys">winged monkeys</a> to attack them; they capture Dorothy and Toto. At the castle, the Witch is stymied by magic when she tries to get the ruby slippers off Dorothy's feet, then remembers that she must be dead first. Toto escapes and leads the Scarecrow, Tin Man, and Cowardly Lion to the castle. After ambushing three Winkie guards, they march inside wearing the stolen guards' uniforms and free her, but the Witch discovers and traps them. The Scarecrow provides a distraction and they attempt to escape, being chased by the Witch and her guards, but are finally surrounded. The Witch sets fire to the Scarecrow and Dorothy puts it out with a bucket of water and unwittingly melts and kills the witch as the water splashes on her. The guards rejoice that she is dead and give Dorothy the charred broomstick in gratitude.</p>
<p>Back at the Emerald City, they bring the broomstick to the Wizard. But when they ask him to keep his promises, the Wizard delays granting their requests much to their shock and frustration. During the argument, Toto pulls back a curtain and exposes the "Wizard" as a normal middle-aged man who has been projecting the fearsome image; he denies Dorothy's accusation that he is a bad man, but admits to being a <a href="/wiki/Humbug" title="Humbug">humbug</a>. He then gives the Scarecrow a diploma, the Lion a medal and the Tin Man a ticking heart-shaped clock, making them realize that they had what they wanted all along. They just did not know it yet. He then prepares to launch his hot air balloon to take Dorothy home but Toto runs off, and as she tries to get him back, the balloon leaves without them. Suddenly, Glinda returns and tells her that she can still return home by using the ruby slippers. After sharing a tearful farewell with her friends, Dorothy follows Glinda's instructions and taps her heels together three times and repeats, "There's no place like home". She wakes up in bed at her home in Kansas, surrounded by her family, the farmhands, Professor Marvel and Toto. Though they dismiss her adventure as a dream, she insists that it was all real, and that there is no place like home.</p>
