<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Film_Institute_lists">American Film Institute lists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: American Film Institute lists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> (AFI) has compiled various lists which include this film or elements thereof.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Movies" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Movies">AFI's 100 Years...100 Movies</a> – No. 6</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Thrills" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Thrills">AFI's 100 Years...100 Thrills</a> – No. 43</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Heroes_%26_Villains" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Heroes &amp; Villains">AFI's 100 Years...100 Heroes &amp; Villains</a>:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wicked_Witch_of_the_West" title="Wicked Witch of the West">Wicked Witch of the West</a> – No. 4 villain</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Songs" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Songs">AFI's 100 Years...100 Songs</a>:
<ul>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Over_the_Rainbow" title="Over the Rainbow">Over the Rainbow</a>" – No. 1</li>
<li>"<a href="/wiki/Ding-Dong!_The_Witch_Is_Dead" title="Ding-Dong! The Witch Is Dead">Ding-Dong! The Witch Is Dead</a>" – No. 82</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Movie_Quotes" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Movie Quotes">AFI's 100 Years...100 Movie Quotes</a>:
<ul>
<li>"Toto, I've a feeling we're not in Kansas anymore." (Dorothy Gale) – No. 4</li>
<li>"There's no place like home." (Dorothy) – No. 23</li>
<li>"I'll get you, my pretty – and your little dog, too!" (Wicked Witch of the West) – No. 99</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_Greatest_Movie_Musicals" title="AFI's Greatest Movie Musicals">AFI's Greatest Movie Musicals</a> – No. 3</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Cheers" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Cheers">AFI's 100 Years...100 Cheers</a> – No. 26</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years...100_Movies_(10th_Anniversary_Edition)" title="AFI's 100 Years...100 Movies (10th Anniversary Edition)">AFI's 100 Years...100 Movies (10th Anniversary Edition)</a> – No. 10</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_10_Top_10" title="AFI's 10 Top 10">AFI's 10 Top 10</a> – No. 1 <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_film" title="Fantasy film">Fantasy film</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_honors">Other honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>1999: <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 100 Maverick Movies – No. 20.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></li>
<li>1999: <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 100 Greatest Films – No. 32.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
<li>2000: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 100 Best Films of the 20th Century – No. 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li>2002: <i><a href="/wiki/Sight_%26_Sound" title="Sight &amp; Sound">Sight &amp; Sound</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Greatest Film Poll of Directors – No. 41.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></li>
<li>2005: <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Film" title="Total Film">Total Film</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 100 Greatest Films – No. 83.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></li>
<li>2005: ranked among the top ten of the <a href="/wiki/BFI_list_of_the_50_films_you_should_see_by_the_age_of_14" title="BFI list of the 50 films you should see by the age of 14">BFI list of the 50 films you should see by the age of 14</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li>2007: <i>Total Film</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 23 Weirdest Films – No. 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></li>
<li>2007: <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> ranked the film's songs and music at the top of its list of 50 greatest film soundtracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guard_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-guard-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Differences_from_the_novel">Differences from the novel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Differences from the novel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Roughly 40 identifiable major differences exist between the original book and the MGM interpretation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequels_and_reinterpretations">Sequels and reinterpretations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sequels and reinterpretations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Adaptations_of_The_Wizard_of_Oz" title="Adaptations of The Wizard of Oz">Adaptations of The Wizard of Oz</a></div>
<p>The film was dramatized as a one-hour radio play on <i><a href="/wiki/Lux_Radio_Theatre" title="Lux Radio Theatre">Lux Radio Theatre</a></i>, which was broadcast on December 25, 1950, with Garland reprising her earlier role. In 1964, a one-hour animated cartoon called <i><a href="/wiki/Return_to_Oz_(TV_program)" title="Return to Oz (TV program)">Return to Oz</a></i> was shown as an afternoon weekend special on NBC.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> An official 1974 <a href="/wiki/Sequel" title="Sequel">sequel</a>, the animated <i><a href="/wiki/Journey_Back_to_Oz" title="Journey Back to Oz">Journey Back to Oz</a></i> starring <a href="/wiki/Liza_Minnelli" title="Liza Minnelli">Liza Minnelli</a>, daughter of Garland, was produced to commemorate the original film's 35th anniversary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1975, the stage show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wiz" title="The Wiz">The Wiz</a></i> premiered on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadway_theater" title="Broadway theater">Broadway</a>. It was an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">African American</a> version of <i>The Wizard of Oz</i> reworked for the stage. It starred <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_Mills" title="Stephanie Mills">Stephanie Mills</a> and other Broadway stars and earned a number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">Tony Awards</a>. Its financing was handled by actor <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Holder" title="Geoffrey Holder">Geoffrey Holder</a>. Its inspired revivals after it left the stage and an unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/The_Wiz_(film)" title="The Wiz (film)">motion picture</a> made in 1978, starring <a href="/wiki/Diana_Ross" title="Diana Ross">Diana Ross</a> as Dorothy and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> as the Scarecrow.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 1985, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Productions</a> released the live-action fantasy film <i><a href="/wiki/Return_to_Oz" title="Return to Oz">Return to Oz</a></i>, which starred (and introduced) <a href="/wiki/Fairuza_Balk" title="Fairuza Balk">Fairuza Balk</a> as a young Dorothy Gale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Based loosely on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marvelous_Land_of_Oz" title="The Marvelous Land of Oz">The Marvelous Land of Oz</a></i> (1904) and <i><a href="/wiki/Ozma_of_Oz" title="Ozma of Oz">Ozma of Oz</a></i> (1907), it fared rather poorly with critics who were unfamiliar with the <i>Oz</i> books and was not successful at the box office, although it has since become a popular <a href="/wiki/Cult_film" title="Cult film">cult film</a>, with many considering it a more loyal and faithful adaptation of what L. Frank Baum envisioned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geraghty_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geraghty-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1995, Gregory Maguire published the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Wicked_(Maguire_novel)" title="Wicked (Maguire novel)">Wicked: The Life and Times of the Wicked Witch of the West</a></i>, which was adapted into the wildly successful Broadway musical <i><a href="/wiki/Wicked_(musical)" title="Wicked (musical)">Wicked</a></i>. The story describes the life of the Wicked Witch of the West and other events prior to Dorothy's arrival.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>For the film's 56th anniversary, a 1987 stage show also titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1987_musical)" title="The Wizard of Oz (1987 musical)">The Wizard of Oz</a></i> was based upon it and the book by L. Frank Baum. It toured from 1995 to 2012, except for 2004.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2005, <a href="/wiki/The_Muppets_Studio" title="The Muppets Studio">The Muppets Studio</a> produced <i><a href="/wiki/The_Muppets%27_Wizard_of_Oz" title="The Muppets' Wizard of Oz">The Muppets' Wizard of Oz</a>,</i> a television film for <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>, starring <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(singer)" title="Ashanti (singer)">Ashanti</a> as Dorothy, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Tambor" title="Jeffrey Tambor">Jeffrey Tambor</a> as the Wizard, <a href="/wiki/David_Alan_Grier" title="David Alan Grier">David Alan Grier</a> as Uncle Henry, and <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a> as Aunt Em. <a href="/wiki/Kermit_the_Frog" title="Kermit the Frog">Kermit the Frog</a> portrayed the Scarecrow, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Great_Gonzo" title="The Great Gonzo">Gonzo</a> portrayed the Tin Thing (Tin Man), <a href="/wiki/Fozzie_Bear" title="Fozzie Bear">Fozzie Bear</a> portrayed the Lion and <a href="/wiki/Miss_Piggy" title="Miss Piggy">Miss Piggy</a> portrayed all the Witches of the West, East, North and South.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2007, <a href="/wiki/Syfy" title="Syfy">The Sci-Fi Channel</a> released the three-part miniseries <i><a href="/wiki/Tin_Man_(miniseries)" title="Tin Man (miniseries)">Tin Man</a></i>, a science fiction continuation starring <a href="/wiki/Zooey_Deschanel" title="Zooey Deschanel">Zooey Deschanel</a> as DG.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lloyd_Webber" title="Andrew Lloyd Webber">Andrew Lloyd Webber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice" title="Tim Rice">Tim Rice</a> wrote a <a href="/wiki/The_Wizard_of_Oz_(2011_musical)" title="The Wizard of Oz (2011 musical)">stage musical of the same name</a>, which opened in 2011 at the <a href="/wiki/West_End_theatre" title="West End theatre">West End</a><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a href="/wiki/London_Palladium" title="London Palladium">London Palladium</a>. It features all of the songs from the film plus new songs written by Lloyd Webber and Rice. Lloyd Webber also found <a href="/wiki/Danielle_Hope" title="Danielle Hope">Danielle Hope</a> to play Dorothy on the reality show, <i><a href="/wiki/Over_the_Rainbow_(2010_TV_series)" title="Over the Rainbow (2010 TV series)">Over the Rainbow</a></i>. Another production opened in December 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Ed_Mirvish_Theatre" title="Ed Mirvish Theatre">Ed Mirvish Theatre</a> in Toronto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> A reality TV show, also titled <i><a href="/wiki/Over_the_Rainbow_(Canadian_TV_series)" title="Over the Rainbow (Canadian TV series)">Over the Rainbow</a></i>, found a Canadian girl, Danielle Wade, to play Dorothy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The Canadian production then began a North American tour in September 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> An Australian tour will begin at the Lyric Theatre, <a href="/wiki/Queensland_Performing_Arts_Centre" title="Queensland Performing Arts Centre">Queensland Performing Arts Centre</a> in November 2017, followed by a season at the <a href="/wiki/Capitol_Theatre,_Sydney" title="Capitol Theatre, Sydney">Capitol Theatre, Sydney</a> beginning December 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>An animated film called <i><a href="/wiki/Tom_and_Jerry_and_the_Wizard_of_Oz" title="Tom and Jerry and the Wizard of Oz">Tom and Jerry and the Wizard of Oz</a></i> was released in 2011 by Warner Home Video, incorporating <a href="/wiki/Tom_and_Jerry" title="Tom and Jerry">Tom and Jerry</a> into the story as Dorothy's "protectors".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> A sequel titled <i><a href="/wiki/Tom_and_Jerry:_Back_to_Oz" title="Tom and Jerry: Back to Oz">Tom and Jerry: Back to Oz</a></i> was released on DVD on June 21, 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>Writer-director Hugh Gross' <a href="/wiki/Independent_film" title="Independent film">independent film</a> <i><a href="/wiki/After_the_Wizard" title="After the Wizard">After the Wizard</a></i>, produced in 2010, relates events after those of the film. It was released to DVD on August 7, 2012.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> released a <a href="/wiki/Spiritual_successor" title="Spiritual successor">spiritual prequel</a> titled, <i><a href="/wiki/Oz_the_Great_and_Powerful" title="Oz the Great and Powerful">Oz the Great and Powerful</a></i>. It was directed by <a href="/wiki/Sam_Raimi" title="Sam Raimi">Sam Raimi</a>, and starred <a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">James Franco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mila_Kunis" title="Mila Kunis">Mila Kunis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rachel_Weisz" title="Rachel Weisz">Rachel Weisz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Williams_(actress)" title="Michelle Williams (actress)">Michelle Williams</a>. It was the second film based on Baum's <i>Oz</i> series to be produced by Disney, after <i>Return to Oz</i>. It was a commercial success and received a mixed critical reception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, now-defunct independent film company Clarius Entertainment released a big-budget animated musical film, <i><a href="/wiki/Legends_of_Oz:_Dorothy%27s_Return" title="Legends of Oz: Dorothy's Return">Legends of Oz: Dorothy's Return</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> which follows Dorothy's second trip to Oz. The film was a <a href="/wiki/Box_office_bomb" title="Box office bomb">box office bomb</a> and was received negatively by critics largely for its plot and unmemorable musical numbers.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_impact">Cultural impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cultural impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Regarding the original Baum storybook, it has been said that "<i>The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</i> is America's greatest and best-loved home grown fairytale. The first totally American fantasy for children, it is one of the most-read children's books ... and despite its many particularly American attributes, including a wizard from Omaha, <i>The Wonderful Wizard of Oz</i> has universal appeal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>The film also has been deemed "culturally significant" by the United States <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a>, which selected it for preservation in the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Registry" title="National Film Registry">National Film Registry</a> in 1989. In June 2007, the film was listed on UNESCO's <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme" title="Memory of the World Programme">Memory of the World Register</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> The film placed at number 86 on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bravo_(US_TV_network)" title="Bravo (US TV network)">Bravo</a>'s <i>100 Scariest Movie Moments</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bravo_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-bravo-103">[103]</a></sup> In 1977, <a href="/wiki/Aljean_Harmetz" title="Aljean Harmetz">Aljean Harmetz</a> wrote <i><a href="/wiki/The_Making_of_The_Wizard_of_Oz" title="The Making of The Wizard of Oz">The Making of The Wizard of Oz</a></i>, a detailed description of the creation of the film based on interviews and research; it was updated in 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ruby_slippers">Ruby slippers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ruby slippers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ruby_slippers" title="Ruby slippers">Ruby slippers</a></div>
<p>Because of their iconic stature,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-SI-105">[105]</a></sup> the ruby slippers worn by Judy Garland in the film are now among the most treasured and valuable <a href="/wiki/Film_memorabilia" title="Film memorabilia">film memorabilia</a> in movie history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The silver slippers that Dorothy wore in the book series were changed to ruby to take advantage of the new Technicolor process. <a href="/wiki/Adrian_(costume_designer)" title="Adrian (costume designer)">Adrian</a>, MGM's chief costume designer, was responsible for the final design. A number of pairs were made, though no one knows exactly how many.</p>
<p>After filming, the slippers were stored among the studio's extensive collection of costumes and faded from attention. They were found in the basement of MGM's wardrobe department during preparations for a mammoth auction in 1970. One pair was the highlight of the auction, going for a then unheard of $15,000 to an anonymous buyer, who apparently donated them to the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a> in 1979. Four other pairs are known to exist; one sold for $666,000 at auction in 2000. A pair was stolen from the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Judy_Garland_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Judy Garland Museum (page does not exist)">Judy Garland Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Grand_Rapids,_Minnesota" title="Grand Rapids, Minnesota">Grand Rapids, Minnesota</a> and remains missing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another, differently styled pair unused in the film was sold at auction with the rest of her collections by owner actress <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Reynolds" title="Debbie Reynolds">Debbie Reynolds</a> for $510,000 (not including the buyer's premium) in June 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact_upon_LGBT_culture">Impact upon LGBT culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Impact upon LGBT culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For information on the film's impact on LGBT culture in America, see <a href="/wiki/Friend_of_Dorothy" title="Friend of Dorothy">Friend of Dorothy</a>.</div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-63">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Brooks, Tim; Marsh, Earle (2003). "Ford Star Jubilee". <i>The Complete Directory to Prime Time Cable and Network Shows 1946 – present</i>. <a href="/wiki/Ballantine_Books" title="Ballantine Books">Ballantine Books</a>. p. 425. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-345-45542-8" title="Special:BookSources/0-345-45542-8">0-345-45542-8</a>. <q>Last telecast: November 3, 1956 ... The last telecast of <i>Ford Star Jubilee</i>, however, was really something special. It was the first airing of what later became a television tradition – Garland's classic 1939 film <i>The Wizard of Oz</i>, with Judy's 10-year-old daughter <a href="/wiki/Liza_Minnelli" title="Liza Minnelli">Liza Minnelli</a> and Lahr (the Cowardly Lion from the film) on hand to introduce it.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Ford+Star+Jubilee&amp;rft.btitle=The+Complete+Directory+to+Prime+Time+Cable+and+Network+Shows+1946+%E2%80%93+present&amp;rft.pages=425&amp;rft.pub=Ballantine+Books&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.isbn=0-345-45542-8&amp;rft.aulast=Brooks&amp;rft.aufirst=Tim&amp;rft.au=Marsh%2C+Earle&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AThe+Wizard+of+Oz+%281939+film%29"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
